analyze my project carefully before we start fixing some of the errors


Here‚Äôs a quick readout of the codebase and the main risk areas I spotted before we start fixing anything:

Stack/routing: Vite + React 18 + TS + Tailwind/shadcn. Client entry uses BrowserRouter and hydrates in prod (src/main.tsx). Server entry does SSR/SSG with StaticRouter, React Query, and react-ssr-prepass (src/entry-server.tsx). Routes live in src/App.tsx, including top-level blog category and post routes (/:category, /:category/:slug) after the fixed pages.
Blog/data: WordPress REST API wrapper in src/lib/wordpressApi.ts; blog mapping/derivation lives in src/lib/blogService.ts and is used across src/pages/Blog*.tsx. Sitemap and prerender scripts call the WP API at build time (scripts/generate-blog-sitemap.js, prerender.js).
Build/prerender: npm run build runs client + server builds then prerender.js, which also generates sitemaps. Prerender fetches blog posts (tries server bundle, then direct WP API) and writes static HTML into dist/**.
Potential problem spots to address first:

Blog category URLs are inconsistent. The live route is /:category (src/App.tsx, links in src/pages/Blog.tsx and src/pages/BlogCategory.tsx), but the blog sitemap writes category URLs as /blog/<slug> (scripts/generate-blog-sitemap.js). Those sitemap entries will 404. Posts use the root-level pattern correctly.
React Query hydration gap. Server rendering fills a QueryClient, but the client creates a fresh QueryClient with no dehydrated state (src/entry-server.tsx vs src/App.tsx). Hydrated pages can flash loading state or trigger hydration warnings‚Äîespecially on prerendered blog pages.
Network dependency during build. prerender.js and the sitemap scripts call the WordPress API; in a restricted or offline environment the build will fail or generate empty data. There‚Äôs a fallback to an empty blog sitemap, but prerender still depends on fetch succeeding.
Service worker caching likely misses built assets. public/sw.js caches hard-coded /assets/box-logo.webp and a couple of images, but Vite fingerprints assets (e.g. assets/box-logo.<hash>.webp), so offline caching won‚Äôt pick them up.
SEO/meta injection is hand-rolled in prerender.js; if Helmet doesn‚Äôt emit a description/title for a route, the script silently inserts nothing. Worth verifying the key pages output real meta tags once we run a build.
Suggested next steps:

Decide the correct blog category URL scheme and align routes/sitemap/canonical links accordingly.
Add React Query dehydration/hydration so SSR/prerendered markup matches the client.
Run a build in this environment to surface concrete errors (may need to stub WP fetches or provide cached data because of network restrictions).
Fix service worker asset paths or broaden the caching strategy after the above.
in my headless blog implementation, I have some blog posts which have a youtube videos embedded. These youtube videos are not being dispalyed on this new website, it is visible on the old wordpress website. I want to fix this to display the videos in the new website (this project)


Converted WordPress embed markup into real YouTube iframes before rendering blog content, so Gutenberg oEmbed blocks now display videos on the new site. Implemented in src/lib/blogService.ts: added a helper to resolve YouTube URLs, replaced wp-block-embed/wp-embedded-content wrappers with responsive iframe markup, and applied this transformation to both post content and excerpts.

Tests not run (not requested). Next steps: load a blog post that previously missed its YouTube video to confirm the embed now appears; if you want, I can add coverage for other providers beyond YouTube.

To see blog posts from the API you‚Äôll need to run the dev server in an environment that can listen on a port.

You can run it locally outside this sandbox with:

export NVM_DIR="$HOME/.nvm" && . "$NVM_DIR/nvm.sh" (ensure nvm is loaded)
npm run dev -- --host --port 5173
Then open http://localhost:5173.
If you want me to try again here, I‚Äôll need permission to bind to a port (or a WSL2/session that allows it). Let me know and I‚Äôll restart the server for you.

You ran a Bash command in PowerShell. Use one of these:

In a Bash shell (WSL/Git Bash):
export NVM_DIR="$HOME/.nvm" && . "$NVM_DIR/nvm.sh"

In PowerShell:

$env:NVM_DIR="$HOME/.nvm"
. "$env:NVM_DIR/nvm.sh"
After loading nvm, still in the project folder run:
npm run dev -- --host --port 5173 and open http://localhost:5173.

how to get the GitHub personal access token (classic)


Here‚Äôs how to create a GitHub Personal Access Token (classic):

Sign in to GitHub on the web.
Go to Settings ‚Üí Developer settings ‚Üí Personal access tokens ‚Üí Tokens (classic).
Click ‚ÄúGenerate new token‚Äù ‚Üí ‚ÄúGenerate new token (classic)‚Äù.
Give it a name (e.g., ‚Äúbox-sparkle push‚Äù), set an expiration (short as possible), and select scopes:
Check repo (covers all repo access you‚Äôll need to push).
Click ‚ÄúGenerate token‚Äù and copy the token shown once. Keep it secret.
Using it (example in Bash/WSL):

export GITHUB_TOKEN=ghp_yourtokenhere
git push -u https://$GITHUB_TOKEN@github.com/mazinadil/box-sparkle-last.git main
You can revoke the token anytime from the same Tokens (classic) page.

I tracked down why the embeds stay blank: the browser is still trying to hit the WordPress API (which is returning 403), so the post content never arrives client-side. I‚Äôve switched the site to serve blog data from a build-time cache instead.

What I changed:

prerender.js: when it fetches WordPress posts during the build, it now writes them to dist/wp-posts.json (static cache for the frontend).
src/lib/wordpressApi.ts: added a static cache loader. In production, the browser will fetch /wp-posts.json from your own domain and serve posts from there; only if that‚Äôs missing will it hit WordPress. This avoids the CORS/WAF block that was leaving iframes empty.
Pushed to main: c725372 Cache WP posts during build and serve from static JSON.

Next steps:

Trigger a new Vercel deploy so the wp-posts.json cache is generated and shipped with the build.
Recheck a post page (e.g., /artists/freeda-band). It should now render content and YouTube iframes without calling WordPress.
If frames are still blank after this deploy, send me one specific post URL and I‚Äôll inspect the cached HTML pattern to adjust the embed converter further.
